  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2d8fb9a3-f2c7-45ce-a2d8-8b2b8080e2a4'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11783314614182707084">This is a great surging novel about the amassing of a colossal fortune, the political power that comes with it, and the operation of a curse laid on an Irish-American dynasty and the ruthless driving man who founded it.<br/><br/>Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh was thirteen years old when he first saw America through a dirty porthole on the steerage deck of The Irish Queen. It was the e</span>
  <span id="freeText11783314614182707084" style="display:none">This is a great surging novel about the amassing of a colossal fortune, the political power that comes with it, and the operation of a curse laid on an Irish-American dynasty and the ruthless driving man who founded it.<br /><br />Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh was thirteen years old when he first saw America through a dirty porthole on the steerage deck of The Irish Queen. It was the early 1850's and he was a penniless immigrant, an orphan cast on a hostile shore to make a home for himself and his younger brother and infant sister. Some seventy years later, from his deathbed, Joseph Armagh last glimpsed his adopted land from the gleaming windows of a palatial estate. A multi-millionaire, one of the most powerful and feared men, Joseph Armagh had indeed found a home. CAPTAINS AND KINGS is the story of the price that was paid for it in the consuming, single-minded determination of a man clawing his way to the top; in the bitter-sweet bliss of the love of a beautiful woman; in the almost too-late enjoyment of extraordinary children; and in the curse which used the hand of fate to strike in the very face of success itself.<br /><br />Once again, Taylor Caldwell has looked into America's roistering past as a setting for a drama of the consequences of savage ambition - and its meaning then and now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11783314614182707084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_49826245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49826245" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/348969-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263568694p2/348969.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49826245?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/348969-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0449018199" href="/book/show/1800163.Captains_and_the_Kings">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/348969-philip?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49826245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7642051767921675132">Taylor Caldwell is largely unknown today, and CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS is virtually the only novel of her left in print in mass-market paperback, and less than a handful are available in oversized paperback editions. But from 1938 (DYNASTY OF DEATH) through her last published novel, ANSWER AS A MAN (1980), Caldwell kept countless readers enthralled with her powerful sagas of ambition and destiny, set during various periods of American and European history (along with a few diversions to Ancient Ro</span>
  <span id="freeText7642051767921675132" style="display:none">Taylor Caldwell is largely unknown today, and CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS is virtually the only novel of her left in print in mass-market paperback, and less than a handful are available in oversized paperback editions. But from 1938 (DYNASTY OF DEATH) through her last published novel, ANSWER AS A MAN (1980), Caldwell kept countless readers enthralled with her powerful sagas of ambition and destiny, set during various periods of American and European history (along with a few diversions to Ancient Rome and Ancient Greece). Her novels were notable for their great emotional depth, as well as her unerring eye for detail - she was often (and justifiably) accused of verbosity, but she was nevertheless a thunderingly good storyteller.<br /><br />CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS is one of her best novels, almost a late-career companion to DYNASTY OF DEATH and NEVER VICTORIOUS, NEVER DEFEATED (1954). Both novels are about men with a passion for success who let no one and nothing stand in the way of achieving it. Caldwell herself called CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS her "Kennedy novel," because the tragic family she chronicles here does indeed resemble that famous family. The novel's central character, Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh, arrives in America from Ireland as a penniless orphan - decades later he's one of America's wealthiest and most powerful men, with one ambition left: to make his son, Rory, the first Catholic president of the United States.<br /><br />CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS is about power - actually, even more than that, it's about the power behind power, the people behind the scenes - bankers, investors, manufacturers - who control politicians and the destinies of nations.<br /><br />I was besotted with CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS as a teenager, and read it four times between 1972 and 1975. I re-read it two years ago, well over 30 years after my last reading, and enjoyed it all over again.<br /><br />If you've never read Taylor Caldwell, CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS is well worth seeking out, along with DYNASTY OF DEATH, TESTIMONY OF TWO MEN, and DEAR AND GLORIOUS PHYSICIAN. With historical fiction once again highly popular, it's time Caldwell was rediscovered.<br /><br />5/12/12: 39 years after it was published, the paperback edition of CAPTAINS AND THE KINGS has gone out of print. It was the last mass-market paperback of a Caldwell title available - end of an era!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7642051767921675132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16621196212017786011">Captains and the Kings, Taylor Caldwell<br/>Captains and the Kings is a 1972 historical novel, by Taylor Caldwell, chronicling the rise to wealth and power of an Irish immigrant, Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh, who emigrates as a penniless teenager to the United States, along with his younger brother and baby sister, only for their parents to die shortly afterwards. Joseph Armagh befriends a Lebanese immigrant, and both are taken under the tutelage of an American plutocrat. An inter-generational saga f</span>
  <span id="freeText16621196212017786011" style="display:none">Captains and the Kings, Taylor Caldwell<br />Captains and the Kings is a 1972 historical novel, by Taylor Caldwell, chronicling the rise to wealth and power of an Irish immigrant, Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh, who emigrates as a penniless teenager to the United States, along with his younger brother and baby sister, only for their parents to die shortly afterwards. Joseph Armagh befriends a Lebanese immigrant, and both are taken under the tutelage of an American plutocrat. An inter-generational saga focusing on the themes of the American dream, discrimination and bigotry in American life, and of history as made by a cabal of the rich and powerful, through Armagh's attempt to make his eldest son, who eventually becomes a senator, the first Catholic President of the United States.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 1984 میلادی<br />عنوان: سران و سلاطین؛ اثر: تیلور کالدول؛ مترجمها: نیره توکلی؛ هادی امین؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، نیلوفر، 1361، در 530 ص، چاپ دوم زمستان 1363؛ چاپ سوم 1372؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی تبار آمریکایی - سده 20 م<br />رمان تاریخی «سران و سلاطین»، اثری از «جانت میریام تیلور کالدول»، نویسنده ی بریتانیایی، که در سال 1972 میلادی، بنگاشته شده است. داستان «سران و سلاطین»، در باره ی یک مهاجر خردسال «ایرلند»ی، به نام «جوزف آرما»، به همراه برادر، و خواهر کوچکتر خویش است. آنها به عنوان مهاجرین غیرقانونی، به امریکا سفر می‌کنند، و مدت کوتاهی پس از کوچ، والدین خود را از دست می‌دهند. «جوزف»، با یک کوچنده ی «لبنان»ی دوست می‌شود، و هر دو زیر سرپرستی آمریکایی ثروتمندی، دل به کار می‌دهند. داستان یک دلاوری رخداده و پیوسته ی میان نسلی ست، که بر روی سوژه هایی همچون: «تاریخ»، «رؤیای آمریکایی»، «برتری نژادی» و «هواداری بیش از اندازه» در زندگی مردمان آمریکا، تکیه دارد، که توسط یک قشر آسوده و ثروتمند ساخته شده‌ است. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_116952821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116952821" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/926958-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420861609p2/926958.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116952821?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/926958-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780002211307" href="/book/show/183793.Captains_and_the_Kings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116952821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15812444829600878498">I don't even know where to start with this book. My dad told me about it years ago. Its not exactly one you find lying around on library shelves waiting to be checked out. And, in fact, I only have a copy because I borrowed it from my dad... and HE only has a copy because my sister found it at a thrift store. Anyway- back to reviewing it.<br/><br/>First- beware it is what I call "old" writing. What I mean by that is it is more of a Margaret Mitchell or MM Kaye style than say a modern day popular author. I</span>
  <span id="freeText15812444829600878498" style="display:none">I don't even know where to start with this book. My dad told me about it years ago. Its not exactly one you find lying around on library shelves waiting to be checked out. And, in fact, I only have a copy because I borrowed it from my dad... and HE only has a copy because my sister found it at a thrift store. Anyway- back to reviewing it.<br /><br />First- beware it is what I call "old" writing. What I mean by that is it is more of a Margaret Mitchell or MM Kaye style than say a modern day popular author. It has details that most people would skip and yet are so vital and contain information pertinent to the story that you must read them in order to understand. <br /><br />Next- it is set in the mid-1800s to earlier 1900's and full of politics, yet while reading it, I still felt as though I was reading the politics of today. It forces you to question and wonder and be suspicious. I quite enjoyed that haha however, if you are already prone to conspiracy theories, this might put you over the edge.<br /><br />Furthermore- the character development is intense. I think that's part of what I distinguish as "old" writing, where the author spends more time letting you into why their characters are doing things as opposed to describing what they actually did. And there are so many characters, that takes time and pages! (hello- this thing is over 800 pages long!) I was so impressed with her ability to keep her characters true to themselves and what she had established, but allowing them to grow with the story and circumstances she developed. <br /><br />Finally- my dad will tell you he thinks this story is loosely based on the Kennedy Family. Do I agree? hmmmm... possibly. The author has obviously changed the time period and circumstances enough so that if it wasn't planted in your mind already, you may not make the connections. However, I can see that it might be inspired by their heritage. <br /><br />Overall, it was a great read. Its got me thinking about black helicopters and skulls and societies. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15812444829600878498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer197801600" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14590076448763186602">A truly extraordinary book in every way! My mom told me that a long time ago, she read a book that was so good, and I thought to myself, I have to read this. I enjoyed every page, and it's amazing to think about how it applies to our lives today. If you read it and think about it, the book should both frighten you while making you wonder who the hell is actually running our country and the world. Men behind curtains that no one has ever heard of making decisions that change how the world functio</span>
  <span id="freeText14590076448763186602" style="display:none">A truly extraordinary book in every way! My mom told me that a long time ago, she read a book that was so good, and I thought to myself, I have to read this. I enjoyed every page, and it's amazing to think about how it applies to our lives today. If you read it and think about it, the book should both frighten you while making you wonder who the hell is actually running our country and the world. Men behind curtains that no one has ever heard of making decisions that change how the world functions, all for political and economical gain that furthers their push for abosolute power. <br /><br /><br /><br />I highly recommend anyone willing to turn on their brains give this a try with an open mind. You will no regret it. Five stars is all I can give but I would have given more.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10852090456718219298">Ok--Be very careful with Taylor Caldwell books. She has geared these toward women who want hardcore romance--if you know what I mean. It is usually brief I hear, but the point of her books is not about "heaving bossoms" it's to educate the average reader about governments and what goes on behind the scenes. She is very educated and a very talented writer and usually writes about a specific conspiracy. They may sound strange but I would highly recommend any of her books (minus the bedroom scene) </span>
  <span id="freeText10852090456718219298" style="display:none">Ok--Be very careful with Taylor Caldwell books. She has geared these toward women who want hardcore romance--if you know what I mean. It is usually brief I hear, but the point of her books is not about "heaving bossoms" it's to educate the average reader about governments and what goes on behind the scenes. She is very educated and a very talented writer and usually writes about a specific conspiracy. They may sound strange but I would highly recommend any of her books (minus the bedroom scene) for anyone interested in learning politics without getting out a history book. </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14276660643908688782">For everyone who did or has ever voted in a presidential election, this is a must read. When an unknown can come out of the woodwork, unstudied and untested, without any sort of litmus test, and become our president, we must ask ourselves, "Who is he and who owns him?' Read this book! It is haunting!</span>

<div id="review_431683990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/431683990" />
    <a title="Valeria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12379046-valeria"><img alt="Valeria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351114684p2/12379046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/431683990?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valeria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valeria" href="/user/show/12379046-valeria">Valeria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer431683990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12832870983612826585">Captains and the Kings is such a great all around read in my opinion. So much so that it is one of my favorite books of all time (and that's saying a lot coming from me). <br/><br/>While the theme at first glance seems to be a rags to riches story, it goes so much more beyond that. You have history, romance, politics, drama (plenty of it yet not overdone), and it also delves into the different natures of human beings. It is easy to read, yet pretty intense and I had a difficult time putting this book down</span>
  <span id="freeText12832870983612826585" style="display:none">Captains and the Kings is such a great all around read in my opinion. So much so that it is one of my favorite books of all time (and that's saying a lot coming from me). <br /><br />While the theme at first glance seems to be a rags to riches story, it goes so much more beyond that. You have history, romance, politics, drama (plenty of it yet not overdone), and it also delves into the different natures of human beings. It is easy to read, yet pretty intense and I had a difficult time putting this book down! Caldwell writes so well and is able to captivate the reader that by the end of the book, I was left wanting more. <br /><br />For those who haven't read this book yet, I hope you give this one a chance!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12832870983612826585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43653907-alan"><img alt="Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438413139p2/43653907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alan" href="/user/show/43653907-alan">Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781504039" href="/book/show/34992916-captains-and-the-kings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3519123914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1932190625440677546">An epic novel that will no doubt charm conspiracy theorists who read it. For me, a timely read in light of US politics today. Well written, if a little repetitive on some of its key themes but made powerful through the author’s steadfast stance on the universality of corruption in industry, politics and the lives of society’s powerful elite. Quite a large meal, this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1879036355" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1879036355" />
    <a title="Ange H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21166492-ange-h"><img alt="Ange H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509888949p2/21166492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1879036355?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ange H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ange H" href="/user/show/21166492-ange-h">Ange H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32947303-captains-and-the-kings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1879036355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18233863915594924710">This sweeping saga of a powerful family dynasty, loosely based on the Kennedys, was written in the 70's, but it could be a cautionary tale published yesterday about political corruption and the dangers of socialism. It was actually quite depressing, in the context of what is going on in our country today, so it took me awhile to get through. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_88476113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88476113" />
    <a title="LemonLinda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1541888-lemonlinda"><img alt="LemonLinda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604612189p2/1541888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88476113?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LemonLinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LemonLinda" href="/user/show/1541888-lemonlinda">LemonLinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88476113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9098589814472205892">This is a pretty powerful HF from the early 70s. Caldwell was quite a prolific writer. This is one of her later books which was made into a popular mini-series in the 70s. On the surface it is a book of a young Irish immigrant who with hard work and a willingness to do whatever was needed for success was able to build a multi-million dollar business empire and to consort with the world's most powerful people. Joseph Armagh closely resembles Joe Kennedy in his Irish heritage, his interest in poli</span>
  <span id="freeText9098589814472205892" style="display:none">This is a pretty powerful HF from the early 70s. Caldwell was quite a prolific writer. This is one of her later books which was made into a popular mini-series in the 70s. On the surface it is a book of a young Irish immigrant who with hard work and a willingness to do whatever was needed for success was able to build a multi-million dollar business empire and to consort with the world's most powerful people. Joseph Armagh closely resembles Joe Kennedy in his Irish heritage, his interest in politics, his determination to see his son elected to the American presidency, and his ruthlessness. Yet he was also a loving and caring brother, father and business partner and lover, but those feelings never came first. First and foremost he had a vision of how to succeed, how to get even and how to advance his own personal agenda.<br /><br />So on one level this is the personal story of Joseph Armagh and how he overcomes so many obstacles in his fight to provide for his "family". But on another level it is written with a flagrant political agenda - to expose the presence of "an invisible government", a world-wide gathering of bankers, businessmen, etc. who collectively decide " the destinies of nations, their survival or their obliteration", who is elected, who is assassinated, what their political agenda will be, etc. Both sides of the story help to make this one a most intriguing read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9098589814472205892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1097293-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347053570p2/1097293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2432978082?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/1097293-barbara">Barbara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32947303-captains-and-the-kings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2432978082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13331741611009712989">Since my grandparents immigrated to the USA in the mid/late 1800s I love reading historical fiction shining light on the ocean travel across the Atlantic and then the determination and independent hardwork necessary to become prosperous American citizens. The beginning of this novel was very enjoyable but the rambling filler throughout this novel turned the reading enjoyment into a grueling task just to finish reading this book.<br/>I did finish this it because I made a promise to myself to always fi</span>
  <span id="freeText13331741611009712989" style="display:none">Since my grandparents immigrated to the USA in the mid/late 1800s I love reading historical fiction shining light on the ocean travel across the Atlantic and then the determination and independent hardwork necessary to become prosperous American citizens. The beginning of this novel was very enjoyable but the rambling filler throughout this novel turned the reading enjoyment into a grueling task just to finish reading this book.<br />I did finish this it because I made a promise to myself to always finish any book that I start reading but I honestly had to drag myself through this one. This is a terrific story with interesting characters but the micro descriptions of storm clouds and wall paneling and fireplace flames and facial expressions and so on stole 2 stars from my review. <br />My analogy is this....When I go to a fine restaurant for an outstanding enjoyable meal I don’t need the chef or waitress to stand at my table telling me every ingredient used, where the spices originated, how they were prepared and how long the meal baked. Would that equate to an enjoyable eating experience? Not to me! I’d consider the meal delicious but definitely not enjoyable. That’s exactly how I feel about reading this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13331741611009712989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_261576600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261576600" />
    <a title="Gerald" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7250653-gerald"><img alt="Gerald" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324872937p2/7250653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/261576600?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerald" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerald" href="/user/show/7250653-gerald">Gerald</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7250653-gerald?shelf=genre-historical-fiction">genre-historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7250653-gerald?shelf=theme-family-saga">theme-family-saga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7250653-gerald?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7250653-gerald?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7250653-gerald?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261576600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11537575092035622942"><i>Captains and the Kings</i> is the sweeping 1972 novel of the family of Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh, who departs Ireland as a 13-year-old with his mother and younger brother Sean to join his father in America. His mother dies upon arrival in New York harbor giving birth to his baby sister Regina. He promises her to take care of the family. They are penniless and find out they will not be allowed to debark in New York at the same time that he is informed that his father has recently died. They debark</span>
  <span id="freeText11537575092035622942" style="display:none"><i>Captains and the Kings</i> is the sweeping 1972 novel of the family of Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh, who departs Ireland as a 13-year-old with his mother and younger brother Sean to join his father in America. His mother dies upon arrival in New York harbor giving birth to his baby sister Regina. He promises her to take care of the family. They are penniless and find out they will not be allowed to debark in New York at the same time that he is informed that his father has recently died. They debark in Philadelphia. Joseph uses most of the little money he has been left by his father to place Sean and Regina with the nuns in an orphanage. Joseph begins working at anything and sends money to the orphanage so they won’t put Sean and Regina up for adoption. He frequently goes hungry because he won’t spend money to himself when it is needed to keep his family together.<br><br>Joseph happens on a newspaper article about an oil strike in Titusville, PA and “borrows” money from his employer (which he later repays with interest) as he leaves without notice for Titusville. During a train accident he saves the life of an injured fellow traveler Harry Zeff, following which he is befriended by a rich and powerful fellow Irishman Ed Healey. Joseph soon becomes indispensable to the wide variety of business interests in which Mr. Healey is involved. This evolves into an almost father-and-son relationship and at Mr. Healey’s death, Joseph becomes the principal heir to the majority of the vast business interests. Now, after fifteen years, Joseph is able to provide a beautiful home for Sean and Regina and takes them from the orphanage. <br><br>The inheritance Joseph received from Mr. Healey was VERY large. Joseph is so driven that he has increased the value many times in the years following. He is a very ruthless businessman and will take all necessary steps to reach his goals. This included threats against the family of a congressman which drove him to commit suicide rather than face the consequences of what Joseph threatened to do. However, the congressman writes Joseph a letter prior to his death in which he places a curse on Joseph’s family. Joseph is not superstitious and does not initially believe in the curse, but as the novel progresses, so many deaths occur to members of his family and others for whom he cares, that the curse begins to haunt him. This becomes especially true when he is financing the effort to get his last living child elected as the American President.<br><br>I well remember the 1976 TV miniseries that was made of this novel and have intended to read it many times. I’m very glad to have gotten the push to do so from the Aussie Readers’ Group, i.e., <b>Book Reading Challenges -&gt; May Challenge - Reduce your TBR list!</b> I barely finished it during the month of May, but do intend to continue the “Reduce my TBR list” effort. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/369110.Captains_and_the_Kings" title="Captains and the Kings by Taylor Caldwell" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1223665320s/369110.jpg" alt="Captains and the Kings by Taylor Caldwell" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/369110.Captains_and_the_Kings" title="Captains and the Kings by Taylor Caldwell" rel="nofollow noopener">Captains and the Kings</a> is a well written very enjoyable family saga. It has many parallels to the Kennedy Clan and their alleged curse. I enjoyed it a lot and recommend it to others who might be interested.<br><br>[Book 45 of revised 2012 target 70 (Jan-10; Feb-11; Mar-9; Apr-8; May-7)]<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11537575092035622942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The common thread of course is mankind with the good and the bad traits shining through! Captains and the Kings was made into a mini-series and CD set is available even now on Amazon. I am going to order the set. After reading the book in the 70's, I gained a great insight not only into the history of the era but also a pretty good portrait of old Joe Kennedy Sr. who was strikingly similar as the chief character of this book. In any event, it was a good read and I would read it again if it were available on Kindle. However, new copies are still available for those who want to settle down with a great book. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12525458791046433024"><br/><br/>If the US today is ruled by corporates that patronise its governments in a way no other country's governments are, there definitely must be some history to this? Turns out there is- and from the days of the pre-abolition pre-suffragette 'democracy' no less. The extent of their power in not just administration but also in king-making hits you hard and strong in 'Captains and the Kings' by Taylor Caldwell. An epic story of a poor Irish immigrant child forced to grow up fast and take the world by t</span>
  <span id="freeText12525458791046433024" style="display:none"><br /><br />If the US today is ruled by corporates that patronise its governments in a way no other country's governments are, there definitely must be some history to this? Turns out there is- and from the days of the pre-abolition pre-suffragette 'democracy' no less. The extent of their power in not just administration but also in king-making hits you hard and strong in 'Captains and the Kings' by Taylor Caldwell. An epic story of a poor Irish immigrant child forced to grow up fast and take the world by the horns. He remain as honest and practical as possible while accumulating enough for at first a comfortable, then a powerful, and then the most visible a life. The author's sensitive pen has an apt phrase for every seemingly contradicting set of emotions and an optimum description for each unique dilemma. <br /><br />The system that benefits you can eat you up ruthlessly. One is reminded of The Old Man and the Sea, which is a mighty compliment to any work of art. The author doesn't like socialism and we are subjected to repeated arguments against it which for a Left-leaner like yours truly, was incredibly amusing :) The author while being understanding of female characters is still in the 19th century where terms like 'crying like a woman' are accepted without a blink. Today we know that conditioning is huge in creating these stereotypes. Minor chinks in the armour... All in all, a journey I'm very glad I undertook. <br /><br />"But the Captains and the Kings haven't departed at all. They are stronger than ever. They will continue to grow in strength until they had the whole silly world, the whole credulous world, the whole ingenuous world in their hands. Anyone who would challenge them, attempt to expose them, show them the unconcealed and naked, will be murdered, laughed at, be called mad or ignored or denounced as a fantasy", thought Tim. "To hell with the world. Maybe these quiet deadly men were all it deserved"</span>
  <a data-text-id="12525458791046433024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15803372906047494713" style="display:none">Joseph Francis Xavier Armagh had a terrible blow in his early life when he emigrated from Ireland to America with his mother and two younger brothers and his mother died on the ship. His father had left before, but upon arriving he found out he was dead too. At 12, he was responsible of his little brother and sister. He found an orphanage for them and he worked in whatever he could, went hungry and suffered as an adult with the hope of reuniting with them, but several years would pass. He was very smart and thanks to his strong, unyielding and pragmatic character managed to access the highest political circles. He felt that the world had betrayed him by taking everything away from him and he would now take his revenge. All his faith was deposited in his eldest son and he would do whatever it took to make him the first catholic president of the United States. We follow the story of Joseph for 70 years in the 19th and 20th centuries. A story of survival and of excellent knowledge of human mind.</span>

  <span id="freeText11227482260689827767" style="display:none">This is a book which I read in the 1970's and I must recommend this book to every American. Doctors cannot treat an illness without diagnosis; an army cannot defeat an enemy without first knowing who the enemy is. Our nation is facing problems that go beyond politics, economics, religion, or beliefs; it is a battle against evil. Read Ephesians 6:12 --spiritual wickedness in high places. This is a story about a poor boy immigrating from East Europe, becomes financially successful and works himself into a powerful position of power and influence. Taylor Caldwell weaves into the story the methods used to gain power and the mistakes and pitfalls that the populace make. Our country right now is experiencing 'pressure from below' in the form of riots and 'pressure from the top' in the form of government controls. Can this people learn from history? This method has been used in the past in the destruction of free people in other countries falling to communist control. Our copy is underlined and marked throughout--unusual for a fictional book. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1938202556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12812259010027748127">DO NOT BUY THE KINDLE VERSION OF THIS BOOK!!!! I read and enjoyed Taylor Caldwell when I was in high school, so when I found Captains and the Kings for a Kindle $1.99 special, I thought this was a sure hit. I could not have been more wrong. The first third of the book was gripping, despite me gritting my teeth over the complete lack of punctuation or random punctuation in spots where no comma or quotation mark ever should have been. Then it began to seem like chunks of the book were missing. And</span>
  <span id="freeText12812259010027748127" style="display:none">DO NOT BUY THE KINDLE VERSION OF THIS BOOK!!!! I read and enjoyed Taylor Caldwell when I was in high school, so when I found Captains and the Kings for a Kindle $1.99 special, I thought this was a sure hit. I could not have been more wrong. The first third of the book was gripping, despite me gritting my teeth over the complete lack of punctuation or random punctuation in spots where no comma or quotation mark ever should have been. Then it began to seem like chunks of the book were missing. And perhaps these chunks really were! I think whoever formatted this book for Kindle was on drugs. For example, in one chapter Katherine is dying and asking Joseph to marry Bernadette, and in the next screen they refer to Rory as if I am supposed to know who Rory is. Given Taylor Caldwell's detailed descriptions that go on for pages, I found it very puzzling that the wedding and subsequent birth of Rory would be completely omitted. I suspect it wasn't Caldwell, but the fault of whoever was turning the book into Kindle. And from there it just went downhill. I found myself bewildered as to who people were, what had happened during time gaps, and finding more and more excuses not to continue reading. And finally I just gave up at about 52% or so. If I can find a paper copy someday at a used book fair, I will start it over and probably really enjoy the book. But the Kindle version is appalling. I'm glad I paid only $1.99.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12812259010027748127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3326296854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17844703840253144531">I’d like to call this book a psychological thriller without the thriller part. Every character is over analyzed ad nauseam. It was a good story but way too long. The main character, Joseph, a 13 year old Irish immigrant, is both the protagonist and antagonist. His whole goal in life is making money. In the beginning it was important because he had two younger siblings to care for. Then he was compelled to constantly prove himself. He pushed his son into politics and intended him to be president.</span>
  <span id="freeText17844703840253144531" style="display:none">I’d like to call this book a psychological thriller without the thriller part. Every character is over analyzed ad nauseam. It was a good story but way too long. The main character, Joseph, a 13 year old Irish immigrant, is both the protagonist and antagonist. His whole goal in life is making money. In the beginning it was important because he had two younger siblings to care for. Then he was compelled to constantly prove himself. He pushed his son into politics and intended him to be president. His family seemed to be cursed as one tragedy after another befell them. I began to wonder how much of this story was reflective of the Joseph Kennedy dynasty. All in all I liked the book, but I listened to almost 35 hours of it and I sped up the narration! Not sure I could have kept up with that much reading! Ha!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17844703840253144531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('44XQ5kyZoDP/PrfdXjG+FVIySsGVJxG8QrNu4WvQ1SF1skQ1Kq3KzFGu/V+p0ccXaKxRo8vGOUcN7XnnpA7wnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Having lost everything due to hyper-inflation, she considers jumping into the freezing waters of the Spree rather than facing the humiliating existence shared by millions of her fellow Germans. However, a chance meeting makes her change her mind at the last moment and offers her a chance to rely on the help of the metropolis itself, where anything can be sold and bought for money and where connections are everything. The bustling nightlife of cosmopolitan Berlin, with its casinos and dance halls, brings good income for the ones who don’t burden themselves too heavily with morals.    After a New Year’s Eve party, Margot finally meets her ever-absent and mysterious neighbor, Paul Schneider, who makes a living by producing a certain type of film for his rich clientele. Under his guidance, Margot discovers a new passion of hers – photography and soon, her talents are noticed by the prominent newspaper, Berliner Tageblatt itself. But being an official photographer of the most celebrated events of the La Scala and most famous Berlin theaters no longer satisfies Margot’s ambitions. As soon as the chance presents itself for her to get involved with the cinematography on the set of &quot;Metropolis&quot; - the film with the highest budget ever produced by the UFA – Margot jumps at it, without thinking twice. At the same time, Paul becomes involved with a rival project, &quot;The Holy Mountain,&quot; which stars an as yet unknown actress and an emerging director in, Leni Riefenstahl. As the two women meet, professional rivalry soon turns into a true friendship, fueled by their passion for cinematography. However, due to the economic woes facing Germany, both projects soon run out of money and now, both film crews must go to extreme lengths to save their respective productions.    Set against the       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/33384.Taylor_Caldwell">About Taylor Caldwell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/33384.Taylor_Caldwell"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1352223619p3/33384.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/33384.Taylor_Caldwell">Taylor Caldwell
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
345
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12799640091739562590"><i> Also known by the pen names Marcus Holland and Max Reiner. </i><br/><br/>Taylor Caldwell was born in Manchester, England. In 1907 she emigrated to the United States with her parents and younger brother. Her father died shortly after the move, and the family struggled. At the age of eight she started to write stories, and in fact wrote her first novel, <i>The Romance of Atlantis</i>, at the age of twelve (although it </span>
  <span id="freeText12799640091739562590" style="display:none"><i> Also known by the pen names Marcus Holland and Max Reiner. </i><br /><br />Taylor Caldwell was born in Manchester, England. In 1907 she emigrated to the United States with her parents and younger brother. Her father died shortly after the move, and the family struggled. At the age of eight she started to write stories, and in fact wrote her first novel, <i>The Romance of Atlantis</i>, at the age of twelve (although it remained unpublished until 1975). Her father did not approve such activity for women, and sent her to work in a bindery. She continued to write prolifically, however, despite ill health. (In 1947, according to TIME magazine, she discarded and burned the manuscripts of 140 unpublished novels.)<br /><br />In 1918-1919, she served in the United States Navy Reserve. In 1919 she married William F. Combs. In 1920, they had a daughter, Mary (known as "Peggy"). From 1923 to 1924 she was a court reporter in New York State Department of Labor in Buffalo, New York. In 1924, she went to work for the United States Department of Justice, as a member of the Board of Special Inquiry (an immigration tribunal) in Buffalo. In 1931 she graduated from SUNY Buffalo, and also was divorced from William Combs.<br /><br />Caldwell then married her second husband, Marcus Reback, a fellow Justice employee. She had a second child with Reback, a daughter Judith, in 1932. They were married for 40 years, until his death in 1971.<br /><br />In 1934, she began to work on the novel Dynasty of Death, which she and Reback completed in collaboration. It was published in 1938 and became a best-seller. "Taylor Caldwell" was presumed to be a man, and there was some public stir when the author was revealed to be a woman. Over the next 43 years, she published 42 more novels, many of them best-sellers. For instance, <i>This Side of Innocence</i> was the biggest fiction seller of 1946. Her works sold an estimated 30 million copies. She became wealthy, traveling to Europe and elsewhere, though she still lived near Buffalo.<br /><br />Her books were big sellers right up to the end of her career. During her career as a writer, she received several awards.<br /><br />She was an outspoken conservative and for a time wrote for the John Birch Society's monthly journal <i>American Opinion</i> and even associated with the anti-Semitic Liberty Lobby. Her memoir, <i>On Growing Up Tough</i>, appeared in 1971, consisting of many edited-down articles from <i>American Opinion</i>.<br /><br />Around 1970, she became interested in reincarnation. She had become friends with well-known occultist author Jess Stearn, who suggested that the vivid detail in her many historical novels was actually subconscious recollection of previous lives. Supposedly, she agreed to be hypnotized and undergo "past-life regression" to disprove reincarnation. According to Stearn's book, <i>The Search of a Soul - Taylor Caldwell's Psychic Lives</i>, Caldwell instead began to recall her own past lives - eleven in all, including one on the "lost continent" of Lemuria.<br /><br />In 1972, she married William Everett Stancell, a retired real estate developer, but divorced him in 1973. In 1978, she married William Robert Prestie, an eccentric Canadian 17 years her junior. This led to difficulties with her children. She had a long dispute with her daughter Judith over the estate of Judith's father Marcus; in 1979 Judith committed suicide.<br /><br />Also in 1979, Caldwell suffered a stroke, which left her unable to speak, though she could still write. (She had been deaf since about 1965.) Her daughter Peggy accused Prestie of abusing and exploiting Caldwell, and there was a legal battle over her substantial assets.<br /><br />She died of heart failure in Greenwich, Conn</span>
  <a data-text-id="12799640091739562590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
